0525423656|5.0|Ally Condie does it again. Her writing style is so lyrical and fluid, her storytelling so heartfelt and inspirational.  I think those reviewers who objected to the use of poetry actually reinforce one of the story's themes: people appreciate, value, and seek that which is denied them. Many of us live in societies where it's easy to take for granted the treasure troves of great poetry, literature, history, art, music, etc., readily available in libraries, museums, schools, stores, and online. If Cassia and Ky had our access to all of this, they probably wouldn't be so affected by centuries-old poetry either. But that's the point. Their circumstances, their struggles against the limited knowledge and freedom of the Society open them up to the shared human experience of these lines of verse that transcend time and place. Ally captures that concept in an amazing way, weaving it through the pages, making it a symbol of the characters' rebellion, and inviting the reader to be part of that connection too.  Crossed builds substantially on the foundation of Matched. We learn more about the main characters and the world. We meet interesting new characters and see interesting new places. Some mysteries resolve while others deepen. I did feel that Ky's and Cassia's \\"voices\\" weren't distinct enough and sometimes had to flip back to the chapter headings to figure out who was talking. But overall, the quality of the writing is awesome. I love the imagery and emotion of Ally's words, as well as the intrigue and premise of the story. I would like to know more about the Society, its leader(s), its motivations, its rationalizations, and its purpose. Why do they do what they do? Hopefully these questions will be addressed in the next installment.  This is an enjoyable, thought-provoking book...wish I could keep reading to the end right now instead of having to wait another year!

B000002UAI|4.0|It is nice to see the predecessor to Rubber Soul display such a subtle switch in maturity and attitude from the smiling, wiggling moptops people were trying to write off back during their earlier output.  Considering this album was released the year I was born and having grown up in a household of 2 out of 3 siblings who preferred them to the likes of Bobby Sherman (don't ask), the matter of mono verses stereo isn't even an entity here.  Great music is great music, even if you have to get out your grandparents' old 78s to hear Glenn Miller the way he truly sounded.  The music will surpass the technology if it's truly great, and this is my argument with For Sale.<br /><br />Moodier than their earlier albums, one tends to rely on interviews with John Lennon from Beatle Brunch and other such Sunday morning radio shows for, not only how tired they appear on the album cover, but also their less than happy-go-lucky sound this time out.  I heard recordings of John explaining why the Beatles stopped touring and it was truly an eye opener.  To be in their position and have a bipolar reaction of love and hate to that magnitude would truly change your approach in the studio as well.  It shows a young group of brilliantly 20-somethings who were battling critical analysis by the press, blackmailings by wealthy politicians for favors to their kids, and teen idolization Lennon enjoyed least of all of them to show how grace still held under pressure once being hurried back into studio for a Christmas release.<br /><br />1. \\"No Reply:\\"  A bitter song about cheating with among the finest melodic structures in all of pop-dom to this day, it stands as one of their truly great pre-hippie tracks that doesn't detract appeal to the fans of their earlier catalog.<br /><br />2.  \\"I'm a Loser:\\"  Some self-deprecating reflection from Lennon?  Again, just like on the previous track, his voice is strong and emotive, and the song is an inarguable classic.  I still laugh about the parody of the song by the Mosquitos on Gilligan's Island, regardless of the fact they looked and sounded more like the Byrds.<br /><br />3.  \\"Baby's in Black:\\"  Gorgeous harmonies between Lennon and McCartney with a mid-tempo rhythm that gets you lazily bobbing to it without much thought.<br /><br />4.  \\"Rock and Roll Music:\\"  This has never been my favorite classic early rock song, but I don't understand what people have against the cover either.  It's certainly better than others I've heard, especially the vomit-inducing REO Speedwagon.<br /><br />5. \\"I'll Follow the Sun:\\"  Not quite as depressing as the above tracks, this is one of the finest and catchiest melodies to ever brace the Beatles songwriting catalog.  It's obviously typical McCartney, and it is the forefather of songs like \\"Lovely Linda\\" and \\"Junk.\\"<br /><br />6.  \\"Mr. Moonlight:\\"  Okay, so it's not that great, I agree.  Compared to crap like Cheap Trick, among their most awful imitators, though, this is a brilliant cover.<br /><br />7.  \\"Medley:  a) Kansas City/b) Hey, Hey, Hey, Hey:\\"  Great rockin' covers with road roughened bawlz.  This shows just what a great grasp they had on R&B as a covers group, and their own pop melodies never detracted from the fact that they never lost that grittiness even later.<br /><br />8.  \\"Eight Days a Week:\\"  Sorry, but this has never been my favorite Beatles song at all, but I don't dislike it either.  It sounds like it was written in a hurry, but to their credit, I would never have dreamed of a title like that.  Hell, it's even become a catch phrase!<br /><br />9.  \\"Words of Love:\\"  Interesting Buddy Holly cover.  It's Lennon and McCartney's harmonizing here that keep your attention forward and center.<br /><br />10.  \\"Honey Don't:\\"  They should have applied the title of this song as a response to the idea of letting Ringo sing lead on it.  He has his cute novelty moments, but this one just doesn't work.<br /><br />11.  \\"Every Little Thing:\\"  Outstanding!  Easily my favorite cut onthis album.  It's short, sweet, has upbeat lyrics and a sweet sentimentality that detracts from it's alleged datedness.  It is a truly magnificent, endearing timepiece that stands still in my book.<br /><br />12.  \\"I Don't Want to Spoil the Party:\\"  My second favorite track on FS, we used to play this song all the time on the stereo when I was little, and it brings back some really great memories.  A bit Everly Brothers-like, the harmonies are stellar and the simple, folk pop arrangement is also very sharp.<br /><br />13.  \\"What You're Doing:\\"  Great rocker.  Polar opposites in depressing and fun, featuring some of Paul's strongest lead vocals and great guitar work by George.  Ringo's puctuative drumming is also very striking on this one.<br /><br />14.  \\"Everybody's Trying to Be My Baby:\\"  Disappointingly standard cover, this one shows the boys were rushed to reach their deadline.  I wouldn't mind it so much if it weren't the last track on the disc.  It would have been better if they'd switched it with \\"I'll Follow the Sun,\\" so that the album could have had a very strong, positive ending cut.<br /><br />Minor flaws aside, this is a very good, strong Beatles effort that shows grace under pressure, and anyone who gives this album less than 4 stars isn't hearing what makes it so phenomenally great.  It is truly the beginning of a new sort of growth for a quartet of young men who probably matured a lot more quickly than they'd intended and, in their creative labor, we fans reaped the rewards.  Five decades later, it's obvious that the rewards of their efforts are very sweet indeed.It is a truly magnificent, endearing timepiece that stands still in my book.  12.  \\"I Don't Want to Spoil the Party:\\"  My second favorite track on FS, we used to play this song all the time on the stereo when I was little, and it brings back some really great memories.  A bit Everly Brothers-like, the harmonies are stellar and the simple, folk pop arrangement is also very sharp.  13.  \\"What You're Doing:\\"  Great rocker.  Polar opposites in depressing and fun, featuring some of Paul's strongest lead vocals and great guitar work by George.  Ringo's puctuative drumming is also very striking on this one.  14.  \\"Everybody's Trying to Be My Baby:\\"  Disappointingly standard cover, this one shows the boys were rushed to reach their deadline.  I wouldn't mind it so much if it weren't the last track on the disc.  It would have been better if they'd switched it with \\"I'll Follow the Sun,\\" so that the album could have had a very strong, positive ending cut.  Minor flaws aside, this is a very good, strong Beatles effort that shows grace under pressure, and anyone who gives this album less than 4 stars isn't hearing what makes it so phenomenally great.  It is truly the beginning of a new sort of growth for a quartet of young men who probably matured a lot more quickly than they'd intended and, in their creative labor, we fans reaped the rewards.  Five decades later, it's obvious that the rewards of their efforts are very sweet indeed.

The potential was there, but it was more like the plot was just a series of events happening to one-dimensional characters, rather than them living the plot.<br />Second, Darcy is pretty much a wimp in this book, taking little to no action and continually second-guessing himself. Elizabeth seems to exist solely to worry about Darcy.<br />Third, and this is nit-picky, but the author has a habit of providing backstory by having characters discuss previous events (that both characters were party to and of which they are therefore fully aware) in excrutiating detail that is just too awkward for words. B000EHSVSC|4.0|Americans never really understood how they were dragged into World War I during the period from 1914 to 1918; and the horrors that humanity went through in that period, in which thirteen million people lost their lives, made the United States, which, like the rest of the world, was to suffer further horrors in the Great Depression of the 1930s, wary of entering international conflicts that had nothing to do with them.  Even the rumblings from Adolf Hitler in Germany meant nothing to the U.S.--for a while, anyway.  When Japanese emperor Hirohito ordered a surprise attack on America's Pacific Fleet at Pearl Harbor, Hawaii on December 7, 1941, however, America woke up to a new kind of reality, as World War II was bought to their very doorstep.  This was the story told with frightening accuracy, from both sides of the conflict, in the multi-national 1970 World War II epic TORA! TORA! TORA!  Based on Gordon Prainge's book \\"Tora! Tora! Tora!\\", and Landislas Farago's book \\"The Broken Seal\\", this well-mounted movie, which, at a cost of $25 million, was among the most expensive films made in Hollywood up to that time, focuses, on the way the Imperial Japanese navy prepared to do what its emperor was ordering of it, and the way the American military staff in Hawaii were trying to understand what they were up to.  The truth of the matter is that America and Japan had both been at odds for some time over various issues; negotiations between the two countries were going on for much of 1941; and if Japan could not get what it considered a fair deal from a country that was still largely considered isolationist and inferior in the eyes of the world, then it would take it all by force.  As far as the American military was concerned, there was no indication that a sneak attack of any kind was imminent on them; and it was assumed diplomacy would work things out.  It then came through a deciphering of secret Japanese communiqu√©s that an attack was under way; but by the time the deciphering was in the hands of the Pacific fleet staff, it was too late.  Pearl Harbor was virtually destroyed in a matter of two hours; numerous battleships, including the Arizona, sank to the bottom; and almost 2,500 people were killed.  It was the greatest single loss of life in any attack on the United States...until September 11, 2001.  It would have been tempting for 20th Century Fox, the studio that funded and distributed this film, to make it a jingoistic piece of propaganda and paint the United States as the victim (even the 2001 blockbuster PEARL HARBOR, a near-enough remake of TORA! TORA! TORA!, flirted with that); but, like on its 1962 classic THE LONGEST DAY, it avoided doing so.  Instead, thanks to the participation of two prominent Japanese directors, along with veteran U.S. director Richard Fleischer (THE BOSTON STRANGLER; FANTASTIC VOYAGE), the film looks at the events leading up to December 7, 1941 from each side of the conflict, with the Japanese, including their revered Admiral Isoroku Yamamoto (Soh Yamamura), anxious to strike but knowing full well what it may mean for their empire in the end, and the Americans misreading Japanese intentions and disregarding the numerous warning signs until they are backed into a corner.  The film gives equal credit to both sides, as befitting as accurate an account of history as Hollywood can muster.  Featuring the Oscar-winning special effects work of L.B. Abbott, A.D. Flowers, and Art Cruickshank, TORA! TORA! TORA! also features solid actors like Jason Robards, Martin Balsam, Joseph Cotten, Richard Anderson, George Macready, James Whitmore, Wesley Addy, Leon Ames, and others rounding out a fine cast, along with Goldsmith's always dependable scoring genius, which here combines American and Oriental themes in a unique way.  By avoiding the romantic sub-plots and the gung-ho theatrics of the Jerry Bruckheimer-produced and Michael Bay-directed PEARL HARBOR, TORA! TORA! TORA!, though an unavoidably lengthy movie, makesitself stay truly memorable in the way it sticks with the historical facts; and it will certainly make the viewer wonder just how certain wars throughout history get started.  In the case of the Japanese attack on Pearl Harbor, which led to six months of victory for them in the Pacific before they were ambushed at Midway in June 1942, it was a combination of misreadings, misunderstandings, and (on the part of the Japanese) the nerves of riverboat gamblers that made history happen.  And as TORA! TORA! TORA! makes abundantly clear, such is often the way history gets made.

B000AS4L16|1.0|As the son of a member of the Polish underground whose unit Zoska was recognized for saving 350 Jews during the 1944 Warsaw Uprising I would like to say that the emotions of my father and myself, after watching the parts of the movie involving Poles, were that of disgust and anger.  This part seemed to us to be patently manipulated to shamelessly further an anti-Polish agenda.  I remember how, as people who speak Polish, and are familiar with the realities of WW II occupied Poland, we felt, as we watched this movie, how the questions posed to the apparently poor, uneducated and unsophisticated Polish villagers were leading, contained double meanings, and/or were taken out of context, and were intended to elicit specific responses.  To boot, we perceived the tone of the translator to be aggressive, rude, manipulative, patronizing, hostile, accusatory and demeaning, while the villagers were clearly being polite, non confrontational, agreeable, welcoming, and basically human to strangers who were to them unlikely visitors to their remote and obscure village. The loss in translation of the subtle nuances of tone, use of specific words, etc. appeared to me and my father to have been deliberately exploited by the director to foster an unflattering image of all Poles.  This, alas, is not something that would be apparent to the non-Polish speaking viewer.  The choice of interviewees, the losses in translation, the omission of Polish suffering as well as the failure to mention positive behavior of Polish Catholics towards Jews, coupled with alleged false facts (I personally do not remember the false claim reported by others to have been allegedly made in the movie that the Polish underground refused to provide arms to the Jewish ghetto), the non-Polish viewer is thereby unsuspectingly left with an unmistakably negative but false and unfair impression of the role and culpability of Poles in the persecution of Jews by the German Nazis.    In summary, I found this work to be insidiously and dangerously misleading, in line with communist propaganda, which in the past sought to undermine any support for a free Poland by encouraging a negative opinion of Poles and Poland.  This movie was, in fact, made and released, while Poland was still on its knees under Soviet control, and in my view, is the moral equivalent of a kick to a person laying unconsciously and helplessly on the ground after an unprovoked severe beating.  I personally believe that Lanzmann's \\"Shoah\\", is unworthy of the subject matter, and needs to be vigorously challenged in the name of common decency, the truth, and most importantly, the memory of the millions of Poles who were killed, forced into slave labor, deported, evicted from their land, tortured, maimed, terrorized and starved during the brutal and inhuman occupation of Poland by Germany in the name of \\"Deutschland, Deutschland Uber Alles\\" and \\"Lebensraum\\" for Germans, the memory which he, Lanzmann, sweepingly maligns.  This movie is insensitive to a nation that did much to defy German Nazism, at extreme cost, from the beginning of WW II until the end.   The subject matter of this movie itself is indeed of monumental importance and interest as it, in and of it self, is extremely sobering, thought provoking, and shocking.  This has little to do with Claude Lanzmann, however.  Any documentary on this subject created in a minimally competent fashion would no doubt elicit the same extreme emotions.  When judging this movie and the contributions of the director, one should assess whether the movie took full advantage of the material, and for what.  I believe the material WAS taken advantage of, but to divide, to gratuitously judge and to shamelessly claim the moral high ground, without having earned the right to do so.  I have such strong feelings on this movie that I would loathe watching it again, even though I can watch other movies on WW II and German crimes against humanity.   PS  I did read that Mr. Lanzmann, in regards to questions on the anti Polish bias in the movie, allegedly stated that had he known what he has since learned about Polish WW II history, he would have done the parts on Poland differently.  If this is true, then the parts of the movie regarding Poland SHOULD BE redone, plain and simple.

B004Z29X3E|5.0|Martha Marcy May Marlene, or \\"M4\\" as I like to call it is one of the best films I've seen this year(I thought the films this year were pretty poor but still)The film follows Martha(Elizibeth Olson) as she desperately makes her escape from a secluded farm in up state New York. She escapes to a nearby town but she's soon confronted by one of her fellow \\"community members\\" from the farm. They share the film's first uncomfortable moment while they eat lunch at the local diner. Martha makes a move for the diner door but he grabs her arm coldly saying \\"what's the matter? you're shake'n\\" then proceeds to leave Martha to her own devices. She's scared and confused but is able to regain her composure enough to call her older sister Lucy(Sarah Paulson).It seems that Martha has being missing for sometime and Lucy is all that remains of her estranged family. Once Martha is reunited with her sister, she attempts to rejoin normal society. Lucy does her best to look after her sister but the mental scars that Martha bares soon become apparent.     As the film progress we get a glimpse into what transpired at the farm. Director T. Sean Durkin choose to hop back and forth from the present to the past to drive the film. Sometimes this approach causes a film to become unfocused or details get muddled but Durkin executes it perfectly. He's slow and methodological with his approach but the slow pace of the film really adds an element of tension that I haven't felt while watching a film for sometime. I found myself clenching my jaw as if watching a speeding car bowling towards an unsuspecting pedestrian.    Aside from superb directing, M4 is supported by fantastic acting. Elizibeth Olsen puts in a strong lead performance as the terrified/mentally ill Martha. She's beautiful and eloquent but her eyes show a deep sadness and unexpressed terror. Sarah Paulson has a solid performance as the well meaning, but overwhelmed and frightened Lucy and John Hawkes channels his inner Charles Manson asthe charismatic cult leader. M4 is a excellent example of a truly unsettling suspense film and a portrait of a troubled and tortured psyche.

0307959856|2.0|Pride and Prejudice is my favorite book.  I've read all of Austen's novels, including the unfinished works and juvenilia.  I have seen every movie adaptation of every one of the works, including Bridget Jones's Diary and Clueless.  I'm not a stickler about any of it.  Love it all.  I even thought Keira Knightly made a surprisingly appealing Elizabeth Bennet.  I've read many of the (uniformly awful) \\"sequels\\" and hated them for the usual reasons: They were either overly sexual (!), overly explanatory about the period, or they brought in coy references to world events or famous people.  Austen never wrote about sex, wouldn't have had to give her readers little lessons in Regency customs, and kept her world very, very tiny.  I just want someone to write an homage that stays true to those qualities!  I don't want Mr. Darcy suddenly becoming a vocal abolitionist or speaking up for feminism.  So I was very excited when I heard about this book.  P.D. James is a famous British author, in her nineties no less, and a lifelong Austen fan, so I hoped for the best.  Also, I love a good murder mystery.  I was very disappointed.  The mystery part of the story is really lame.  There's no subtlety, no finesse.  The hallmark of a good mystery is that when each clue is explained, you say to yourself, \\"Of course!\\"  But here, one of the most mysterious clues (having to do with initials) is explained away in the end by something the reader couldn't possibly have guessed.  The characters didn't ring true at all--Darcy is an emotional, insecure wreck.  She makes mistakes, referring to Mr. Collins as Mr. Bennet's nephew, when he was supposed to be his cousin, and she several times describes Colonel Fitzwilliam as being very handsome, whereas in the original he was described as having an open and pleasing, but not a handsome face.  Which is not a big deal, I guess.  A little disrespectful to be so careless, I think.  But also there's the gothic tone of the novel--all dark and stormy nights and mysterious apparitions and a courtroom denouement complete with last-minute confession.  Jane Austen wouldn't have written such nonsense.  She made fun of gothic novels!    Here's a short list of things that would bug a fan of the original:  She has Fitzwilliam make a joke about Darcy's \\"newfangled water closet\\" (Oh, come on!)  She specifies the names of the horses pulling the carriage (for no reason whatsoever)  She has Darcy, Alveston and Fitzwilliam discuss Mary Woolstoncraft's views on women's rights  She has the characters sympathetically discuss the servants, dwelling on their hopes and aspirations  She has the characters discuss/contemplate the French Revolution and the tyranny against the working classes that brought it about  She has the characters discuss Napoleon  Jane Austen never mentioned the war except to help move her little stories forward.  Her writing was apolitical.  She was of her own time, and didn't have, for God's sake, the perspective of a modern liberal westerner.  Don't get me wrong, I'm a modern liberal westerner.  And Jane Austen, had she been born two centuries later, would undoubtedly have been one too.  But let's keep her in her own time and enjoy her style, and not go messing it up with our newfangled ethos.  It's actually kind of insulting to put modern views and world perspective in the mouths of her characters.  It's a little like apologizing for what Jane Austen was not, instead of celebrating what she was.

B004A8ZWXS|5.0|WAR HORSE conjures up feelings I had when I first read BLACK BEAUTY years ago, the saga of a horse who went from owner to owner amid a series of mostly unhappy circumstances. The difference here is the background (World War I), the luscious farm scenes that start the tale, the colorful faces of the village folk, and at the center of the tale, an earnest and good-looking lad (Jeremy Irvine) who adopts the horse and must turn it into a plow horse so his family can retain their farm.<br /><br />And when the war comes, the grim scenes of battle offer a stark contrast to the sentimental scenes at the start, as the horse proves himself to be a fine specimen until he is caught in a barbed wire situation that requires the assistance of British and German soldiers to put aside the war while they free him from suffering and pain.<br /><br />The usual bombastic score that John Williams gave many of Spielberg's action films is missing here. Instead, there are delicate melodies played brilliantly on flute for the lighter moments and impressive richer sounds for the dramatic highlights. It's a lovely piece of craftsmanship.<br /><br />So is the film, which shows a high level of craftsmanship throughout, the settings and costumes realistic, the performances beyond reproach, and the sentimental happy ending so welcome after all the audience has been through with the brave war horse. Credit must go to Steven Spielberg for his detailed direction and to his cinematographer for the stunning camera work.<br /><br />By all means, one of the best Spielberg films to come along in a long time. Jeremy Irvine is perfectly cast in the leading role and all of the supporting players are well cast, particularly Emily Watson, David Thewlis, Peter Mullan, Neil Arestrup and Benedict Cumberbatch.<br /><br />Solid entertainment, it holds the interest throughout despite its length. Certainly one of the best films of 2011.

0446547654|3.0|The Best of Me is the story of Amanda Collier and Dawson Cole.  Amanda was a pampered princess of their small Southern town and Dawson was from the wrong side of the tracks. Back in the 1980's, they were each other's first love.  After learning that Amanda was accepted to Duke, but her parents wouldn't pay for her to attend if she kept dating Dawson, Dawson broke up with her.  They wouldn't see each other again for twenty-five years.  Dawson was soon after involved in a tragic accident and Amanda moved on with her life with marriage and kids.  After the death of their mentor Tuck, they both end up back in Oriental North Carolina to say goodbye and rediscover each other.<br /><br />While I have enjoyed Sparks books in the past (especially The Wedding), I didn't think this was one of his best.  It was immensely readable and the action kept the plot moving, but the plot seemed like a rehash of previous Sparks novels.  The overall theme for me seemed to be even if you were in a tragic accident beyond your control and you spent your life trying to make up for it, it was never good enough.  That is more than a depressing message.  I also guessed the ending before the end and I didn't like the end.<br /><br />I never felt like I really liked Amanda or Dawson.  I didn't care as much about their love for each other as I should have.<br /><br /> I also didn't like how Amanda and Dawson broke up to begin with.  I guess I figure if you are that in love, you don't have to break up so that Mommy and Daddy can pay for you to go to college.  I thought that was more than a bit lame.  Maybe I am biased since I had to actually work and take out loans to pay for my entire college education myself.<br /><br />I am also usually against novels where there is an affair or leaving of a spouse and your children.  Yet in this case, Amanda has been unhappily married to alcoholic Frank for years.  Although they've gone to counseling and she's talked to Frank about the problem, things do not change.  I guess I'm all for keeping your family together, but when you have your kids living with an alcoholic, I'm not sure you are doing anyone any favors.<br /><br />Tuck was an important part of the book, but I didn't feel that you got to know him that well.  I think there should have been more Tuck.  I also couldn't wait to read the letters he left both Amanda and Dawson, but I thought they were a bit of a let-down when you actually got to read them.<br /><br />Overall, The Best of Me was readable, but I would skip it and read one of Sparks other much better novels such as The Wedding.<br /><br />This review was first published on my blog, Laura's Reviews.nge. Sometimes on songs such as \\"Marry The Night\\",\\"Judas\\",\\"Heavy Metal Lover\\" and the title song there's all too heavy a late 90's [[ASIN:B000002NJS Ray of Light]] period Madonna influence,in addition to the obvious rave/gay club thud Lady Gaga has made something of a trademark. I guess it's being called electropop. Some of that sameness in production is why I deduct one star in the review. However it all plays wonderfully on the club scene however. On \\"Government Hooker\\" there's more of a colder Eurodisco flavor to the production. \\"Americano\\" is one strong number here,incorporating a mixture of tango and Habanero dance rhythms in with the disco dance type music. \\"Bloody Mary\\" is my favorite on the album,a jam on the funkier side of new wave dealing with that delightfully decedent party scene.  \\"Scheibe\\" brings the German connection into it,again as with all these songs telling tales of social outsiders who are proudly \\"born that way\\". On \\"Hair\\" there's this retro wall of sound via E (as in electronic too lol) Street Band sound,appropriately featuring Clerence Clemons on sax. He's also featured on the more poppy \\"The Edge Of Glory\\".<br /><br />  \\"Bad Kids\\",\\"Heavy Metal Lover\\" and especially \\"Electric Chapel\\" with it's rock guitar intro have a somewhat cyberpunk edge to them. \\"You And I\\" is also a fascinating song-kind of a electronic country pop number. It all helps me realize the key to what Lady Gaga is doing with her music here. The filter she looks through is electro rave/dance music. But she brings a lot of the different musical influences that that she embraces into that as well. Musically eclectic artists exists. But they tend to separate their influences out from song to song. Lady Gaga looks into all of her music through that electronic dance filter. Sometimes it's even just outright that. So if your just not too into electronic production,this might not be for you. But for those who chose to hear beyond it to an artists intent,there's really a lot to admire and love about this. During the remainder of the year after this release Lady Gaga has been collaborating on duets with Tony Bennett that show her potential to be expanding her musical filter into another place as well. Listen to these inventive,often cabaret and tin pan alley influenced  compositions even outside the production context it's clear to see that Lady Gaga has more than enough potential to expand and improve on her music as time moves ahead.that delightfully decedent party scene.  \\"Scheibe\\" brings the German connection into it,again as with all these songs telling tales of social outsiders who are proudly \\"born that way\\". 1596432594|5.0|Written in Feynman's own words, this graphic treatment of the physicist's life is generally well done.  I think that those who might not have time to read a detailed book on physics should be able to get the gist of the history of quantum theory, and especially QED (Quantum Electrodynamics), as well as the development of the atomic bomb.  Feynman was, as he observed himself, a curious character who was ever tinkering, ever trying to find out more about how things were constructed.  He got involved not only with physics, but drumming, figure drawing and, toward the end of his life, with going to an obscure Soviet region called Tannu Tuva.  He never lived to see it, but died of cancer prior to getting the permission of the Soviet government.  He suffered several tragedies, including the death of his first wife from TB of the lymphatic system, but he never lost his sense of adventure or wonder.  His life is quite worth reading about and if the reader cannot read Feynman's own books, this is a good substitute.

I was not familiar with Dustin Diaz prior to this purchase (the book popped up in my recommendations based on my other purchases); but apparently giving the detail behind the shot is his \\"thing\\".  That's why I bought it and I will say the information seems reasonably complete.  I haven't yet had time to try to recreate any of the shots for accuracy, but the settings all seem believable.  He has two very basic and very short chapters on 1) gear and 2) inverse square law.  Probably could have skipped them all together; but they are so short they don't really get in the way.  The gear chapter may be helpful if you are very new to this.  Chapter 3 is the rest of the book.  On the left facing page is the finished shot and the right facing page contains the pull back/set up shot.  He gives distances, settings, apertures, lenses, etc. etc.  Like I said, a pretty complete recipe.  As far as the images themselves, some are pretty cool and some are just so-so. Probably the most compelling shot is on the cover (and I like it).  Interestingly enough, I liked some of the pull back shots better than the finished image. Warning: If you are not a fan of tilted horizons, you might not like this book.  I counted at least 15 tilted shots out of about 60.  Picky I know; but it does bug some people.  Some of the shots seem a little soft (for instance Dad's face is a little soft on page 90...but he shot a 5 person stack at F/2 so maybe he wanted that).  Anyway, for $14-$15 I think this book is worth it.  I can't say I learned a great deal from it; but I think some of the shots may inspire me to try a few different things and for that I think it is worth it.

Two age old magicians with differing philosophies using the best students they can find to have a duel they're far too young to understand. Great stuff. Loved the set up. Although the initial setup is brilliant, there's only so many times I can enjoy the description of a circus act or a meal or an outfit. The lead characters were the least interesting element of the story. And after being set up by the world's two great magiciians to have this duel, they never really do anything about it. Great to taste, but not much substance underneath.

The DTS-HD Master Audio 5.1 mix is well done - clear and distinct as a performance such as this should be.    Overall, the \\"New Blood - Live in London\\" blu-ray is a great chronicle easily recommended for Gabriel's career fans.

0756404746|5.0|Okay, I have to say, Patrick Rothfuss is quite possibly the best fantasy writer--not author, mind--I have ever read.  His story isn't the best I've read, but in terms of style and technical ability, I don't think there's anything in the fantasy world like it.  Name of the Wind is different from most other fantasy novels in that it is told from a first-person narrative.  The book is Kvothe, the main character, telling his story to a scribe who has come to him in the midst of some supernatural disturbances in the world.  This different technique made the story flow so much better--no breaks for other characters' points of view--while also creating a sort of suspenseful tension/interest between Kvothe's backstory and the supernatural events happening while he narrates.  The tension between the two makes both more intriguing.  Besides this different storytelling style, Rothfuss is just a plain old great storyteller.  I was instantly sucked in and absorbed in the story that managed to be completely believable despite being a fantasy novel; I was reminded of science fiction, at times.  There are, however, some criticisms I have:  1) The book has very little magic in it, relative to most fantasy novels.  This isn't really a bad thing, but I WAS expecting a fantasy novel.  2) The amount of actual movement the plot makes = 0.  Yup.  The book is basically a young-ish man narrating his crazy/eventful/important life from his childhood until his first couple years at the university.  He doesn't even come close to finishing his narrative (I assume he won't be done until the third book, as he says he will tell the storyteller his story in three days, and this is the first), the main point of his childhood--finding out who the beings were that killed his parents--never resolves in the narrative, and the whole book is basically an introduction.  Despite these shortcomings, the storytelling is, as I said, incredible.  You won't care about the lack of actual progress or the scanty amount of magic in the book, because you will be completely engrossed in the story.  And because of the excellent style and execution, anyone (even literary snobs who usually hate fantasy) will find this book amazing.  Read this book, but don't expect your typical fantasy novel.

B000001GJX|3.0|This is the only time Karajan did the Mozart C minor Mass. Usually on such one-off occasions where Karajan recorded a piece just a single time, he knocked it out of the park. Good examples being Mahler's 5th, R. Strauss's Sinfonia Domestica and Alpine Symphony and Nielsen's Inextinguishable. This Mozart Mass however is not on the same exalted level even though the Penguin Guide recommended it as perhaps the best \\"traditional\\" version. I personally feel that Leonard Bernstein's version with the Bavarian orchestra, which is also on DG, is the better choice for a big, traditional account of this piece.<br /><br />Why does this recording not fully deliver? Let's start with balances. With a huge orchestra and chorus, it is difficult for a conductor to keep everything in the sound picture. The orchestra has a tough time keeping itself in check, blaring over a sea of singers. Throughout the piece, the organ part is barely distinguishable behind a blanket sound of strings and chorus. The soloists don't stand out. Arleen Auger for Bernstein is exemplary, like a angel from heaven. Karajan has Barbara Hendricks, who is fine but not in the same league.<br /><br />Then we have Karajan's tempos, all slow and heavy by today's standards. Not that I mind that but compare it with Bernstein who also has a big conception of the work and still moves much faster, with more drama instead of the high-gloss Karajan treatment. Track 6 is a great case in point, with Bernstein getting through it in 5 and 1/2 minutes while Karajan drags on for 7 and 1/2, a huge discrepancy for just one section of the Credo. The Karajan take sounds grandiose the first time one hears it but it grates on your nerves in later hearings, feels like everyone is moving underwater in diving suits. And yes, the organ on Bernstein's CD is clear and fully part of the aural picture.<br /><br />Not that any of these old school versions will matter much to the period instrument crowd. I am writing this to recommend a more 19th century conception of this music. The Berlin Philharmonic supports the chorus with it's plush underpinnings and DG's remastered sound for this Gold CD is leagues better than the original issue. But there is still a lot of congestion at climaxes. On a more positive note... the cover design for this CD as with many other Karajan Gold discs is fantastic. An artistic and imposing photo and with that Gold foil on top of it. I love it!

0375826742|1.0|In the very first installment of this series, protagonist Eragon and his first tutor/mentor Brom discuss the ancient language and magic. the first spell Eragon ever casts is \\" Brisingr\\" a wildly dangerous beast that unleashes a violent burning fire on the world. Brom then explains how the meaning of the word isn't important, but what it means to the caster. If I were to cast \\"Brisingr\\" in the world of Alagaesia, nothing would happen, because to me, Brisingr means nothing more than sheer boredom.<br /><br />[[ASIN:0756949149 Eragon (Inheritance Cycle (PB))]] by Christopher Paolini was an interesting tale marred by horrendous writing and a so-so pace. Regardless of how rough it was around the edges, the story showed promise. Then, Paolini released [[ASIN:0375840400 Eldest (Inheritance Cycle, Book 2)]], which not only didn't improve upon Eragon, it actually made the problems highlighted in the first book even worse. Eldest had horrible pacing, long chapters filled with little to no action, and page upon page of descriptions of nature.<br /><br />I have this little compulsion-type thing where I *have* to finish a series even if I hate it. So, now, I've gone on to read Brisingr. I am writing this review for many reasons, but one of them is to warn potential readers of the whole series: so far, it has not gotten better. Try your hand at something else.<br /><br />The plot is almost nonexistent. If you look at the summary on the book, you'll read about \\"Oaths Sworn\\" that Eragon must fulfill. This is as exciting as it seems: the first 600 pages of this novel are literally just Eragon doing random tasks that he feels the need to complete because he once swore an oath. This means handing out gold, doing lots of traveling, and even one disturbing instance involving a run-in with an enemy that causes the reader to sympathize more with the victim, and not Eragon, the one dishing out a cruel punishment instead of killing a man.<br /><br />The last 150 or so pages have some plot elements... but nothing huge. Paolini, once again, totally retcons something he had been exploring during Eldest and the beginning of this book, forcibly inserting some history and confusion that doesn't exactly sit right within the series. It's not so much the revelation that bugs me, but the fact that I can see how forced it was on the author's part. Then there's a bloody battle and a Rowling-esque plot device is revealed.<br /><br />As a whole, the continuity is all over the place. People take oaths in the ancient language, only to have the novel reveal that oaths can be broken depending on how somebody feels or if they decide to be nice instead of mean. Nasuada is neither nice to Eragon, nor mean, and all of her conversations with him feel stilted and wooden. One random digression into the woods shows a gemstone of a character named Tenga, who is never mentioned again. Characters pop in and out, Eragon eats meat without regret again, throw in some random, predictable deaths and you get Brisingr.<br /><br />The characterization of Eragon is really starting to take a toll on me. He was a basic, boring stock character in the first volume. In Eldest, he proved annoying, but competent. Now, he is just, for lack of a better term, a jack-ss. First, he awkwardly insists on calling \\"Garrow\\" his father, which is definately off-putting to his usually sympathetic cousin, Roran. Then, wherever he goes, he gets total praise and admiration... for deeds he performed out of sheer luck. Everything he tries to do in Brisingr (From killing the Raz'Zac to flying to Ellesmara) only benefits him, and although the rest of the Varden gets annoyed, they still cheer and give him free things whenever he returns home.<br /><br />One thing horrible in this book is the writing. Paolini showed promise in Eragon, but since Eldest, he has disintigrated even farther. Nobody can use the \\" he wrote this when he was 16\\" excuse anymore. He is now a 20-year old, published author. This is inexcusable. His editor should be fired.<br /><br />For starters: everything is in its extreme. When Rhunon creates a new sword, it is \\"the finest sword [she] has ever forged\\", even though she made it in \\"less than a day\\"-- the shortest time *ever*. Often times, Eragon is absolutely exhausted, moreso than he has ever been before, but he fights the tiredness and the threat of sleep because he must be the strongest in the land to defeat Galbatorix, the most evil rider of all time. Saphira, the only female dragon left, also adores the attention she gets, being the most beautiful creature in the land. Wherever Eragon walks, all the flowers and trees can sense the most amazing presence, something that Arya, the prettiest, smartest, toughest female elf can read.<br /><br />As you can see, it gets really annoying after awhile. \\"-est\\" does not an epic plot make.<br /><br />Next, everything is presented in dreadfully forced archaic language. Every character responds with \\"Aye,\\" because that's remotely scottish sounding and something Tolkein would have done. The dwarves use phrases like \\" mine heart\\" and \\"mine eyes\\" because that sounds ancient and stuff because that's what people under rocks talk like. Then, of course, there is scrubby little Albriech, a tiny farmboy who is uneducated, yet seems to speak as well as Nasuada and King Orrin, two super-powerful diplomats. Why does everyone sound so fancy?<br /><br />In one run-in early on, an enemy starts a conflict by yelling at Eragon, saying \\"Silence, you insolent rascal\\" (182). Kay. Like, I totes mcGotes have that high of diction when I'm infuriated with such a rapscallion as Eragon. JK.<br /><br />(It should be noted here that, oddly enough, Angela the Herbalist is the only character who sounds remotely human, and that is because she is based entirely off of the author's sister.)<br /><br />Finally, Paolini uses totally unnecesary words. On page 719, he writes \\"Eragon stepped forward then and smote one of the crossbars of the portcullis.\\" The highest diction-level readers in the audience will recognize \\"smote\\" as the proper (?) way to conjugate the verb \\"to smite\\" in the past tense. Isn't Paolini smart?<br /><br />Everything in this book is described in long similes. There are birds like fish, anger like red hot molten stuff, tears like diamonds, love like flowers. The most effective authors are clear... not confusing. Some of the battle scenes, in the haste of things like \\"excitement\\" and \\"violence\\", the writing becomes muddled and unclear, oftentimes confusing. Combined with elevated diction, its a wonder anyone knows what is going on anymore!<br /><br />Instead of starting out weak and developing into something unique, this series started out weak and has devolved into something even more cliched than its start. Every new idea introduced is clearly derived from soemthing else. The characters are even more stocky and out of control. I no longer could reccommend this series to anyone in good will.<br /><br />And that, to be honest, makes me sad. As an author, Paolini had so much hope for the future when he publsihed Eragon. Unfortunately, as the series *needed* to be dragged out to four novels because of the *complexity* shown in this novel, I have no hope for [[ASIN:0375856110 Inheritance (Inheritance Cycle, Book 4)]]. Who knows? Maybe with my low expectations, I'll appreciate it more.e. 159420229X|5.0|Who knew that a book on memory would be the most visual experience of my year? Of course any memory expert will tell you that the easiest memories to recall are ones that stand out from the rest. Moonwalking with Einstein is a history of memory and of trying to remember. It's also a partial how-to guide on memorizing unusually long lists of trivial data. One of the most interesting tidbits from the book is how we consider the ability to recall nearly perfectly a good thing and yet those rare individuals whose minds approach a true photographic status are seen as handicapped due to their lessened ability to distinguish the quality of a memory.<br /><br />There's a scene near the end of the book, during the Speed Cards round at the U.S. Memory Championships, where the title of the book comes from. The excitement of this moment is a perfect climax for both the reader and the author's efforts.<br /><br />Given the recent success of a movie like Moneyball (about baseball statistics) I think it's possible that a movie about memory could be a hit as well.

B0012OVFV6|5.0|Santana's second album, featuring Mati Klarwein's painting `Annunciation' as very striking cover-art, was released in September 1970 and followed on from the young band's modestly successful 1969 debut album.<br /><br />The music on `Abraxas' raised the bar with a masterful blend of complex Latino rhythms (salsa, cumbia, merengue) integrated into hard-edged rock numbers, slower ballads and driving instrumentals with inventive time-signatures. It's bursting with energy but at the same time displays a maturity and finesse less evident on the debut album and not recovered until `Caravanserai' (the third album, which followed `Abraxas,' is good but for different reasons).<br /><br />Highlights for most fans would be Carlos's beautiful 2-part guitar ballad `Samba Pa Ti' which just about everyone on Earth recognises; the definitive melodic version of Peter Green's `Black Magic Woman' paired with `Gypsy Queen' with a complex driving rhythm, and the clever instrumental `Incident at Neshabur' which incorporates numerous clever time-signature and tempo changes. Greg Rolie's vocal-and-organ dominated `Mother's Daughter' and `Hope You're Feeling Better' add cornerstones of sing-able hard-rock songs to the album, and the masterfully integrated congas and tablas from Mike Carabello and Jose Chepito Areas add so much to the complex percussive-dominated sound that - paired with Carlos Santana's wailing, soulful guitar - they define the distinctive character of the band.<br /><br />It's beautiful, and in 40 years hasn't aged a day. If you don't know it, you really should give it a listen. It's a great, great album from a dynamic, talented young band at the top of their game, and is a true original. No-one ever really copied Santana's distinctive sound, and they retained a character uniquely their own.<br /><br />The name `Abraxas' BTW was taken from a line in German author Hermann Hesse's book `Demien' (Hesse's mystical writings were very trendy in the 1970s).<br /><br />Production values from the 1970 studio sessions were exemplary and you have several versions of the album to choose from, many of those issued in later years incorporating bonus `live' material - all of it good.values from the 1970 studio sessions were exemplary and you have several versions of the album to choose from, many of those issued in later years incorporating bonus `live' material - all of it good.

B0000062FJ|4.0|Santana's 1969 debut album stands apart from most other rock and pop of the period in deploying a unique fusion of San Francisco rock, Latino rhythms and complex African-influenced percussion. This young band made a big impact with a fresh sound, often fast and furious, full of percussive sophistication overlaid with the young Santana's wailing guitar which quickly became their trademark.<br /><br />Hard-edged songs with more traditional verse-chorus structure are mixed with heavily percussive numbers - sometimes with Spanish-language lyrics as in `Jingo' - and the occasional slower-tempo number like `Treat'. The star track on this album is of course `Soul Sacrifice', the long-playing Latino instrumental rocker which had the 1969 Woodstock festival audience on their feet for 10 minutes, prominently featured in the eponymous film of the event and established the band's reputation with a wider audience.<br /><br />It's instructive to listen to this first studio album from Carlos Santana's young band in the context of their second - and more polished - outing just one year later, `Abraxas'. There are similarities and differences, but you can hear the compositions and editing mature and become rapidly more sophisticated.<br /><br />The three extra tracks not available on the original vinyl are well worth having and, if you're discovering Santana's impressive back catalogue, this is a good place to start.

B004ZNB12O|3.0|For a new listener to Pink Floyd.<br /><br />I am an established Pink Floyd fan, so I don't want to bias this review with the typical, \\"Pink Floyd is an album band and this compilation doesn't do that justice\\".  It may be true, but I want to write this review for those that are potentially new Pink Floyd fans looking to introduce themselves to this wonderful band.<br /><br />First off, Pink Floyd weren't a band of hits.  One could say that only a handful of songs really fit the description of hits.  But, Pink Floyd did have their classic songs, and that is where any Pink Floyd compilation must tread.  They had a lot of classic songs, but it is unfortunate that most compilations don't (and probably can't) get them all into a set.  A set like this becomes further limited as a one disc set.<br /><br />To really try and create a Pink Floyd compilation, you really do need to be a multi-disc set.  Some of Pink Floyd's best songs are epic, and I feel like this album dismisses some of the epic tracks due to the length requirements.<br /><br />The song selection here is not horrible, but as others have noted, it neglects a few albums that did have some great Pink Floyd tracks.  Specifically, I am talking about Animals, Meddle, and Piper at the Gates of Dawn.  It probably wouldn't have been easy to include what could be considered the right songs, but I would argue that songs like Have a Cigar, The Fletcher Memorial Home, and High Hopes could be replaced by songs like One of These Days, Fearless, Sheep, Astronomy Domine, etc.  I have nothing against those three songs that are included, but Have a Cigar leaves a listener one track (maybe 1.5 tracks) short of the whole Wish You Were Here album; tracks from The Final Cut should not take precedence over Animals (I'm guessing length is a factor); and it is just unfortunate that nothing from Meddle is provided.<br /><br />The heavy inclusion of songs from Dark Side of the Moon, The Wall, and Wish You Were Here show the importance of the album in enjoying Pink Floyd.  Yet, this compilation fails here in its sequencing.  If so many songs from those three albums are going to be included, they should be sequenced accordingly.  I realize they are not necessarily sequentially chosen from the original albums, but amongst themselves they would still form better cohesive units than what is provided here.<br /><br />Ultimately, if you are aspiring to be a new Pink Floyd fan, or curious at what the band is about, I suggest looking at some of the other compilations out there. They will have their flaws especially if you read the reviews of Pink Floyd fans who think a hits compilation is blasphemy.  I would recommend [[ASIN:B00005QDW5 Echoes: The Best of Pink Floyd]].  It is a two-disc set that does a better job at covering the whole range of Pink Floyd's output.  It is an album that gives you a window into the early Syd Barrett era to the Roger Waters dominated era, to the Post-Waters era in a fully balanced manner.  It is the type of set that will make it easy to see what each album is about.  Last, I wouldn't count out the option of diving into one of their albums.  This specific compilation is heavily weighted on The Wall, Wish You Were Here, and Dark Side of the Moon because they are the most accessible of what Pink Floyd released.  As such, I'd recommend starting with one of those three as a result. They won't make it easy to choose where to go next, but an actual album does make it easy to see just how great the band was at putting together one cohesive work/album vs. the individual tracks.pilation fails here in its sequencing.  If so many songs from those three albums are going to be included, they should be sequenced accordingly. The software is not of any use to me except for converting vinyl to MP3 - everything else must be done with an audio editor (see Audio Editing below).<br />3. I'm not a fan of MP3's as the end all be all. I would rather have multiple file conversion options, to include WAV and AIFF.<br /><br />The Dime Trick:<br />One problem I had almost immediately was that my records were skipping and producing a lot of static and pops. This was resolved just as easily by placing a dime on the control arm. Static and pops are part of what makes vinyl so great, but before adding the dime, the static and pops were a little too overbearing. The dime brought them back to a nice vinyl quality (thanks for the tip dad!). The skipping was also greatly reduced by adding the dime. In fact, one Dizzy Gillespie album went from skipping in every song to just one skip at the end of the first song... a little magical audio editing and that was completely taken care of.<br /><br />I have ordered the [[ASIN:B0009IGAPW Audio Technica AT6012 Record Care Kit - Includes Record Care Solution, Brush Pad, Storage Base and Adhesive Tape]] so I can correctly clean my records and maybe with a little luck, I can remove the dime from the control arm without sacrificing quality.<br /><br />Audio Editing:<br />As I mentioned before, static and pops are part of what make vinyl so great. But, when you're digitizing your records, it's also good to remove some of the static and minimize the pops. Some people like to remove all of it; I just like to remove some of it.<br /><br />There are numerous software titles available for audio editing. Some are free, like Audacity. Some are not free, like Adobe Audition. Whichever software you choose for editing, you'll only need to learn the absolute basics of how to use it for most of your converted records. Of course, if you're trying to hide skips you'll need more knowledge, but getting rid of dead space before or after a track, and removing pops and static are very, very easy things to do.<br /><br />I only wish the Ion software were more capable, so additional software didn't have to be used for such basic track editing. On the other hand, I understand why Ion has tried to keep their software as easy as the name implies - not everyone is a music nut and having too many track options would probably confuse some of their customers.<br /><br />Overall, I'm quite impressed. I gave it 4 stars because of the limitations with the software. The turntable itself deserves 5 stars.ape]] so I can correctly clean my records and maybe with a little luck, I can remove the dime from the control arm without sacrificing quality.  Audio Editing:  As I mentioned before, static and pops are part of what make vinyl so great. But, when you're digitizing your records, it's also good to remove some of the static and minimize the pops. Some people like to remove all of it; I just like to remove some of it.  There are numerous software titles available for audio editing. Some are free, like Audacity. Some are not free, like Adobe Audition. Whichever software you choose for editing, you'll only need to learn the absolute basics of how to use it for most of your converted records. Of course, if you're trying to hide skips you'll need more knowledge, but getting rid of dead space before or after a track, and removing pops and static are very, very easy things to do.  I only wish the Ion software were more capable, so additional software didn't have to be used for such basic track editing. On the other hand, I understand why Ion has tried to keep their software as easy as the name implies - not everyone is a music nut and having too many track options would probably confuse some of their customers.  Overall, I'm quite impressed. I gave it 4 stars because of the limitations with the software. The turntable itself deserves 5 stars.

(Summary for Teachers)<br /><br />Teachers speak of teaching biology before and after David Attenborough in the United Kingdom. This is based on the impact of his earlier \\"Life on Earth\\" and \\"Living Planet\\" series. A younger David sat down among wild gorillas and personally dove in the Alvin into the abyssal ocean depths. Students held their breath as they came to hear biology in Attenborough's voice. The mere presentation of an animal's or plant's life has little story line.  Attenborough's personal involvement became the story line.  Several generations of students who saw life through his eyes shared his wonder.<br /><br />He has continued to be involved in additional nature series. He still appeared in scenes in \\"First Life\\" (bought by the Discovery Channel and not available in the USA).  But the release of \\"Life\\" and \\"Planet Earth\\" has ensured that biology will continue to be mentally pictured through Attenborough's seasoned voice, just as many generations of Americans viewed world news through the intonations of Walter Cronkite.<br /><br />Two audiences will perceive this high quality footage differently.  For viewers with significant outdoors experience, these smoothly transitioning segments are jaw-dropping. But for those electronics-addicted and nature-deprived youngsters, many of these scenes will lack \\"awesomeness\\" since the animation world has no constraint of being anchored to reality.<br /><br />Attenborough is no longer seen on-screen but his voice holds these ten programs together. 2) in Kenya, three male cheetahs take down an ostrich by hunting as a team; 3) Madagascar chameleon uses tongue to capture many insects from a distance, in slow motion; 4) Antarctic crabeater seals versus orca killer whales; 5) open ocean shoals of fish are decimated by swordfish while flying fish take to the air to evade predators; 6) brown-tufted capuchins in Brazil use rock and anvil to crack mature palm seeds; 7) Venus fly-trap has hairs, two must be touched within 20 seconds to trigger closure; 8) stalk-eyed fly in Malaysia emerges from pupal case and its eyes must grow apart in males, showing their use in combat; 9)in dry season in Zambia, hippopotamuses move to deeper river areas and males fight for dominance; 10) courtship of Oregon grebes concludes with beautiful \\"dance\\"; 11) Northwest Pacific octopus lays eggs in den and cares for its eggs until it dies; 12) Costa Rican poison arrow frog moves each of six tadpoles to canopy, each to a separate bromeliad and then repeatedly returns to provide an unfertilized egg as food; 13) fledgling chin strap penguins in Antarctica must make their first swim while a leopard seal takes a few as a meal; 14) orangutan mother and baby.  ON LOCATION: features the challenge of filming in the Antarctic using a sailboat and HMS Endurance's helicopters; challenge of filming leopard seal  underwater up close; also tracking killer whales and filming a seal that makes a miraculous escape.<br /><br />REPTILES AND AMPHIBIANS 1) Introduction to Komodo Island and the Komodo dragons with males in combat during mating season, but more at the end of this program; 2) a brief set of cameos show the diversity of reptiles and amphibians; 3) South American waterfall toad free falls away when pursued by a snake, while a pebble toad hunted by a tarantula tumbles downhill like a rubber ball; 4) on the Pantanal, pools concentrate caiman crocodiles but when the rain returns, fish swim into their waiting mouths [slight error referring to reptiles as cold-blooded rather than ectothermic]; 5)the basilisk lizard perches on branches over streams and when threatened drops to the stream and walks on water; 6) a Brazilian pygmy gecko is so small it has problems with rain drops but uses its hydrophobic surface to become unsinkable; 7) a panther chameleon has grasping toes, turret eyes and ever-changing skin colors; 8) in the Namib dessert, a female chameleon searches for a mate; 9) Canadian red-sided garter snake emerges on snow, while many males emerge seeking to copulate with the female but one late-emerging male mimics the female chemistry and induces warm males to warm it as well; 10) Madagascar collared iguana lays eggs in sand and buries them but a hognosed snake locates and eats them; 11) Sonoran Desert horned lizard female guards her eggs and drives off a smaller snake, then bluffs a coachwhip snake; B0060ZJ7BC|4.0|I know little about baseball, but I quite liked this movie. It is the true story about how Oaklands Athletics manager Billy Beane (a fine performance by Brad Pitt), facing the loss of some of his best players after the end of the season, and with very little budget to hire good replacements, decided to apply statistical methods to find good but undervalued (and therefore, cheap) players. By traveling this path, he gets the opposition of much of the official baseball establishment (though this should not be exaggerated). To help him in this endeavor, he hired a young university graduate (played by Jonah Hill) to whom he soon becomes a mentor, introducing him to the business side of baseball. With these methods, Beane assembled a team for the following season that, while was unable to win the championship, did make it to the playoffs, and generally did much better than expected initially.  The filmmakers are honest enough not to show Beane as a completely nice guy. He has a bad temper. He is cold and aloof with the players (he never travels with the team), refusing to become friends with them, in order to be easier to fire them. It is hinted that he wasn't that good as a husband. Despite these flaws, he is a compelling, generally sympathetic character.  The movie basically believes that human intuition (in the form of the aging scouts) is no match for the mathematical and statistical methods of young nerds. If one has the romantic notion that not everything in life can be quantified, and that in some fields the human brain can still do better than a computer, then one feels oneself to be on the other side of the argument proposed by this movie.  Also, although I'm not very knowledgeable about baseball, it seems to me that the changes proposed by Beane (no stolen bases, emphasis on reaching first base and not taking unnecessary risks) makes for a duller, if more standardized, game. So whether the end result of these changes he proposed made for a more entertaining game, it is debatable.  But despite the fact that I was a bit uncomfortable with its thesis, I did like and enjoy the film.
B001C4AFOY|5.0|This movie is different from the various films done about Queen Victoria in that it focuses on her earlier life as a princess and her early reign as Monarch.  While it doesn't go into great depth about the succession and who is who, we do get a glimpse into what her life was like under the influence of her mother, the Duchess of Kent and Conroy as they tried not only to shelter her but to take advantage of her youth and inexperience and try to force her to make her mother the regent.  Albert enters her life as a potential suitor but he becomes much more and turns out to be her ally and confidante.  The chemistry between Emily Blunt as Victoria and Rupert Friend as Albert was evident in all the scenes, especially when they are playing chess and being watched by the various advisers in the room.  Victoria speaks of herself as a pawn and Albert tells her that she must learn to play the game better than the people who are trying to control her.  We see the frustration that Albert experiences in early marriage when he feels \\"like a guest\\" rather than a husband and partner.  Victoria learns to rely more on Albert for assistance in her duties and of course, this is the all time great love story especially in the era when arranged marriages were just that.  There was definitely love and devotion in this union.  It was sad that Albert died at such a young age and Victoria mourned him for the rest of her life.  As usual with British films the sets were splendid and the 19th century clothing and hairstyles were wonderful and accurate! The other element that I thought was well done was that they  showed  Albert in his native environment speaking German(English Subtitles.)  I don't think I've ever seen this in another film about Albert and Victoria.  After all German was his first language!

B0011HF6GE|5.0|This album absolutely destroyed me. A good friend of mine gave me several albums to borrow a few months back, and while i put them all on my itunes, it took me a while to get around to all of it. One day, while in art class, i decided i would listen to some new music while i was finishing a drawing. I moved my usual very social self to the corner of the room and by chance decided that the album i would listen to today would be Bon Iver's \\"For Emma, Forever Ago.\\" 30 seconds later i was frozen in my seat. by the end of the first chorus of the album opener \\"Flume,\\" my eyes were staring wide open at absolutely nothing, and my jaw was limp. Needless to say, i didnt finish my drawing that period. About a week later i went out and bought a hard copy of this album, because i simply had to own it for myself.  What Justin Vernon has crafted with this is a rarity. It feels utterly familiar and nostalgic, yet at the same time breathtakingly fresh and original. It is the rawest music i've ever heard. The album even seems to change with time. I first discovered it around the late spring/early summer time, and ive found it to be a totally new experience listening to it now that it is winter. If you don't know the backstory to the recording of this album, i recommend you wikipedia it. It makes the experience that much more powerful.   Most songs consist of Veron singing layered falsetto vocals over simple acoustic guitar chords, and some songs add little touches of miscellaneous percussion, horns, or ambient lead guitar here and there. The lyrics are fairly open to interpretation, and they have this amazing impressionistic quality to them. After a few listens, you can determine what almost all the songs are about in a very general sense, but the specifics are up to you.   I discovered this album at a really big time in my life; i was graduating high school, leaving behind old friends and creating new ones, clinging on to relationships with girls and mentors while being thrust intoa new city with new friends and new opportunities. This album really personified all of my bittersweet memories, fears and anxieties about the future, and love for the people i was leaving unlike anything else ive ever listened to. Each song has the power to take you not only back to when you first heard it, but certain songs take me back to certain times before i had even heard of Bon Iver, bring back certain smells and sounds i had almost forgotten. I dont know how it works, this album just drains me emotionally. \\"Skinny Love\\" is the perfect description of trying to hold on to a relationship thats been broken. \\"Re:stacks\\" is an absolutely beautiful song about coming to terms with your feelings for someone. \\"The Wolves\\" is the most powerful song about pain and suffering ive ever heard.   This is not an album to play at a party. It is not an album to get stoned to. I think the first time you listen to this album you should be by yourself, maybe on a long car ride or something. Listening to the album in its entirety is a must. Its an album to listen to completely sober, ready to confront your own personal demons and reflect on your past relationships, both good and bad, and push forward into a new future. 5 stars out of 5.   All of Bon Iver's other music is definitely worth a listen too. check it out.

There were a lot of foreign references and name dropping that was confusing. Don't let this discourage you. Once the story got going it was much clearer and really hooked me.  Mikael Blomkvist, a financial journalist, is in the midst of a scandal. With no prospects and facing some jail time, he accepts an offer to look into a 40 year old mystery; the disappearance of a young girl. Blomkvist does well on his own, but later enlists the help of a talented but strange investigator with issues of her own. I loved considering all the scenarios and trying to figure out the mystery along with the characters. The author made me feel as though I actually came to know Mikael Blomkvist and Lisbeth Salander and I look forward to meeting them again in the other books. While writing this review I checked Amazon for some information about the book and author and was saddened to find out that Stieg Larsson died in 2004.

1552095258|5.0|I had been eyeing this book for a little longer than a year.  Upon receiving it, I was pleasantly surprised by an easy-to-read volume that weaves a bit of history into a discussion of the various aspects of paddle making.  You'll find discussions of everything from paddle designs to the characteristics of the various woods that may be used for paddle construction and a review of the kinds of tools you'll need to make a paddle.<br /><br />If you're looking for an absolute guide that walks you through specific steps to make one of a set number of paddles (e.g., a step-by-step instruction manual to make a specific design), you're looking at the wrong book (though it could be used in that manner).  Rather, the authors try to impart the knowledge that will teach you the overall paddle-making process, but then they leave a lot up to you.  You can stick to the templates in the book and use them to make a simple one-piece paddle, or you can use them as the starting point for making something that varies (a lot, or a little) from the designs contained therein.<br /><br />The book contains a lot of useful information about the subtler aspects of paddle making: the balance point, wood selection, wood matching, and many other topics. It also contains a list of contacts for purchasing suitable lumber.  [I've not had reason to use any of them, but I'm sure they'll be useful to some.]<br /><br />I've long had a desire to craft a paddle that is just right for me.  This book is the means of my pursuit of that desire.  If you've ever wanted something different from those paddles you find on racks at outdoor stores and outfitter shops, and are willing to put in a bit of time to make one, this book is a great place to begin.<br /><br />TOOLS?<br />------<br />While the book reviews the kinds of tools you can use, it spends little time providing instruction in how to use them.  Rather, it provides tips on how best to to use the tools you choose (e.g. how to establish two square edges if working with a planer, how a plane or spokeshave interacts with the wood grain), and provides some great instruction on making jigs and templates that will make your paddle-making easier.  If you are fortunate enough to have a band saw and a belt sander, you'll have some real advantages in your paddle making.  However, you can craft a paddle with basic hand tools (e.g., coping saw, combination square, rasps, planers/draw knives/spokeshaves, sandpaper), so don't think you need a garage full of gadgets to get started.<br /><br />OVERALL<br />-------<br />Even if you never plan to make your own paddle, if you love paddling, you'll find this to be a wonderful book. If you do have an interest in paddle making, this book is a great place to start.e interacts with the wood grain), and provides some great instruction on making jigs and templates that will make your paddle-making easier.  If you are fortunate enough to have a band saw and a belt sander, you'll have some real advantages in your paddle making. The narrator is Max Morden, thought you have to look pretty hard to find it out.  He is telling  the story of his life of those he loved, so to speak, and, at times, others mention his name.  Once his mother asks why his future wife calls him 'Max' your name is ________., and he only says that that is the name he writes under, so that is the name she knows him by.   Max had a bad family life growing up and admits he may have not even loved his parents.  His Dad ran off, leaving his Mom and him to fend for themselves.  The main thrust of this story takes place in some seaside village, Ballyless, which is near Ballymore, where his parents rent a chalet for the summer holidays.  I would have called it a cabin.  I do not think it had running water and maybe not electricity.  The others of this story, the Graces, rented a house with all that and more.  He made friends with the Grace's children.  They were all about the same age, my guess is twelve (12), but they may have been as young as nine (9) or ten (10).   He also tells of his marriage to Ann, their child,. Claire, and how Ann died.  You develop the understanding he is still grieving for his wife who passed away shortly before he starts to tell this story.  The sadness is that he does not realize he is still grieving.  He is just going through motions and doing things, and you realize that he has not recovered form the loss yet, but tries to act like he has.  It sad to witness.   Another third of this story was written  of his life now, at the home of the Graces, the Cedars.  He has rented a room there, as does another gentleman, the Colonel.  It is late in the season, October, so the Colonel and him are the only tenants, along with the landlady.   This such a queer story in his writing style and the subject.  I read it because I wanted to see how it would end.
